### Quick Overview

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/index

On Polymarket, you can buy and sell shares representing future event outcomes (i.e. “Will TikTok be banned in the U.S. this year?”). Shares in event outcomes are always priced between 0.00 and 1.00 USDC, and every pair of event outcomes (i.e. each pair of “YES” + “NO” shares) is fully collateralized by $1.00 USDC. Shares are created when opposing sides come to an agreement on odds, such that the sum of what each side is willing to pay is equal to $1.00. The shares representing the _correct, final outcome_ are paid out $1.00 USDC each upon market resolution. Unlike sportsbooks, you are not betting against “the house” – the counterparty to each trade is another Polymarket user. As such, shares can be sold before the event outcome is known_ (i.e. to lock in profits or cut losses), and _there is no “house” to ban you for winning too much._

--------------------------------

### Quickstart > Quick Start > 2. Place an Order

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/quickstart

To place a limit order, use the `createAndPostOrder` method. You need to provide the `tokenID` (obtainable from the Gamma API), the desired `price` per share, the `size` (number of shares), and the `side` (either `BUY` or `SELL`). The response will include the `orderID` once the order is successfully placed.

--------------------------------

### What is Polymarket? > Quick Overview

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/get-started/what-is-polymarket

On Polymarket, you can buy and sell shares representing future event outcomes (i.e. "Will TikTok be banned in the U.S. this year?"). Shares in event outcomes are always priced between 0.00 and 1.00 USDC, and every pair of event outcomes (i.e. each pair of "YES" + "NO" shares) is fully collateralized by $1.00 USDC. Shares are created when opposing sides come to an agreement on odds, such that the sum of what each side is willing to pay is equal to $1.00. The shares representing the *correct, final outcome* are paid out $1.00 USDC each upon market resolution. Unlike sportsbooks, you are not betting against "the house" – the counterparty to each trade is another Polymarket user. As such, shares can be sold before the event outcome is known (i.e. to lock in profits or cut losses), and there is no "house" to ban you for winning too much.

### Glossary > Market

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/quickstart/introduction/definitions

A single event outcome. Corresponds to a pair of CLOB token IDs(Yes/No), a market address, a question ID and a condition ID.

--------------------------------

### Gamma Structure > Detail > Event

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/gamma-structure

An Event contains a set of markets. There are two variants of events: an Event with 1 market (resulting in an SMP) and an Event with 2 or more markets (resulting in an GMP).

--------------------------------

### Place Multiple Orders (Batching) > Request Payload Parameters

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/create-order-batch

An `order` object is the form:

- `salt`: random salt used to create unique order
- `maker`: maker address (funder)
- `signer`: signing address
- `taker`: taker address (operator)
- `tokenId`: ERC1155 token ID of conditional token being traded
- `makerAmount`: maximum amount maker is willing to spend
- `takerAmount`: minimum amount taker will pay the maker in return
- `expiration`: unix expiration timestamp
- `nonce`: maker's exchange nonce of the order is associated
- `feeRateBps`: fee rate basis points as required by the operator
- `side`: buy or sell enum index
- `signatureType`: signature type enum index
- `signature`: hex encoded signature

--------------------------------

### Place Multiple Orders (Batching) > Response Format

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/create-order-batch

- `success`: boolean indicating if server-side err (`success = false`) -> server-side error
- `errorMsg`: error message in case of unsuccessful placement (in case `success = false`, e.g. `client-side error`, the reason is in `errorMsg`)
- `orderId`: id of order
- `orderHashes`: hash of settlement transaction order was marketable and triggered a match

--------------------------------

### Gamma Structure > Detail > Market

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/gamma-structure

A Market contains data related to a market that is traded on. It maps onto a pair of clob token ids, a market address, a question id and a condition id.

### Your First Order

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/quickstart/orders/first-order

For the Typescript client, after installation, you'll initialize it with the host, chain ID, signer (your private key), and optionally API credentials, signature type, and funder. The `signatureType` can be 1 for Magic/Email login, 2 for Browser Wallet login, or 0 for EOA. You can then use `createAndPostOrder` by providing an order object with `tokenID`, `price`, `side`, `size`, and `feeRateBps`. You'll also need to provide market-specific details like `tickSize` and `negRisk` (true/false) obtained from the `get-markets` API endpoint. Finally, specify the `OrderType`, such as `OrderType.GTC`.

--------------------------------

### Resolution > UMA Optimistic Oracle Integration > Resolution Process > Actions

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/resolution/UMA

Anyone can then propose a price to the question on the OO. To do this they must post the `proposalBond`. The liveness period begins after a price is proposed.

--------------------------------

### How to Fetch Markets > 2. Fetch by Tags

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/fetch-markets-guide

Tags provide a powerful way to categorize and filter markets. You can discover available tags and then use them to filter your market requests. The general tags can be found using the `GET /tags` endpoint, while sports tags and metadata are available via the `GET /sports` endpoint. The `/sports` endpoint returns comprehensive metadata for sports including tag IDs, images, resolution sources, and series information. Once you have tag IDs, you can use them with the `tag_id` parameter in both markets and events endpoints.

--------------------------------

### Order Attribution > Signing Methods > Remote Signing (Recommended)

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/order-attribution

The optional `token` parameter allows you to add an authorization header to requests sent to your signing server, providing an additional layer of security.

--------------------------------

### OpenAPI > Markets API > Sports > Get sports metadata information

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/api-reference/sports/get-sports-metadata-information

The `/sports` endpoint retrieves metadata for various sports. This metadata includes details such as the sport identifier, a URL to the sport's logo or image asset, a URL to the official resolution source for the sport (e.g., league website), preferred ordering for sport display, a comma-separated list of tag IDs for categorization and filtering, and a series identifier linking the sport to a specific tournament or season. The response is a list of sports metadata objects containing this configuration data.

--------------------------------

### How to Fetch Markets > Best Practices

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/fetch-markets-guide

When fetching individual markets, always use the slug method for optimal performance. For category browsing, utilize tag filtering to minimize the number of API calls. If you need to discover all available markets comprehensively, employ the events endpoint combined with pagination. It is recommended to always include `closed=false` in your requests unless you specifically require historical data. For production applications, it is crucial to implement rate limiting to respect API usage policies.

--------------------------------

### How Are Markets Created? > Submit your market proposal

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/how-are-markets-created

To submit a market proposal and increase its chances of being listed, provide comprehensive information including the market title, the designated resolution source, and evidence of trading demand. The most effective channels for proposing new markets are the #market-suggestion channel on Discord or by tagging @polymarket on Twitter/X.

--------------------------------

### How to Fetch Markets > 3. Fetch All Active Markets > Pagination

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/fetch-markets-guide

For fetching large datasets of markets or events, pagination is essential. You can use the `limit` and `offset` parameters to control the number of results per page and the starting point for each subsequent request. For example, setting `limit=50` will return 50 results per page, and `offset=0` starts from the beginning. For the next page, you would increment the offset by the limit value (e.g., `offset=50` for the second page). This applies to both general event fetching and tag-filtered market requests.

--------------------------------

When you have an open order, you'll find it displayed just below the Order Book on the market's page. If you have open orders across multiple markets, you can easily manage and monitor them all from the Portfolio page.

### RTDS Crypto Prices > Message Format > Binance Source Message Format

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-crypto-prices

Messages received when subscribed to the Binance crypto prices (`crypto_prices`) stream have a specific structure. They include the topic, type, a main timestamp, and a payload. The payload contains the symbol (e.g., `solusdt`), a timestamp for the price data, and the `value` which is the current price.

### Resolution > UMA Optimistic Oracle Integration > Resolution Process > Actions

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/resolution/UMA

Binary CTF markets are initialized via the `UmaCtfAdapter`'s `initialize()` function. This stores the question parameters on the contract, prepares the CTF and requests a price for a question from the OO. It returns a `questionID` that is also used to reference on the `UmaCtfAdapter`. The caller provides: `ancillaryData` - data used to resolve a question (i.e the question + clarifications), `rewardToken` - ERC20 token address used for payment of rewards and fees, `reward` - Reward amount offered to a successful proposer. The caller must have set allowance so that the contract can pull this reward in., `proposalBond` - Bond required to be posted by OO proposers/disputers. If 0, the default OO bond is used., `liveness` - UMA liveness period in seconds. If 0, the default liveness period is used.

--------------------------------

### RTDS Crypto Prices > Message Format > Chainlink Source Message Format

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-crypto-prices

Messages from the Chainlink crypto prices (`crypto_prices_chainlink`) stream follow a defined structure. Each message includes the topic, type, a main timestamp, and a payload. The payload contains the symbol in slash-separated format (e.g., `eth/usd`), a price timestamp, and the `value` representing the current price.

The `signatureType` parameter specifies the wallet type; `0` is for standard Ethereum wallets like MetaMask, `1` is for Polymarket's Magic Link users, and `2` is for Gnosis Safe or injected providers.

--------------------------------

### Transaction States

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/relayer-client

Transactions move through the following states: `STATE_NEW` (received by relayer), `STATE_EXECUTED` (executed onchain), `STATE_MINED` (included in a block), `STATE_CONFIRMED` (confirmed/final), `STATE_FAILED` (failed/terminal), and `STATE_INVALID` (rejected/terminal).

--------------------------------

### Comment Hierarchy

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-comments

Comments support nested threading. Top-level comments have a null or empty `parentCommentID`. Reply comments have a `parentCommentID` that contains the ID of the parent comment. All comments are associated with a `parentEntityID` and `parentEntityType`.

--------------------------------

### Authentication Headers

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/order-attribution

The builder signing process adds the following headers to each order request: `POLY_BUILDER_API_KEY`, `POLY_BUILDER_TIMESTAMP`, `POLY_BUILDER_PASSPHRASE`, and `POLY_BUILDER_SIGNATURE`. These headers are automatically generated and attached by the SDK, so you do not need to construct them manually.

--------------------------------

### Onchain Order Info

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/onchain-order-info

The `makerAmountFilled` represents the quantity of the asset that the maker has given out during the fill. The `takerAmountFilled` signifies the quantity of the asset that the taker has received. Finally, the `fee` field indicates the fees that were paid by the order maker as part of this transaction.

--------------------------------

### Steps

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

The calculation begins with the quadratic scoring rule for an order, based on its position between the adjusted midpoint and the minimum qualifying spread. This forms the basis for subsequent scoring steps.

--------------------------------

### Resolution > UMA Optimistic Oracle Integration > Clarifications

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/resolution/UMA

Recent versions (v2+) of the `UmaCtfAdapter` also include a bulletin board feature that allows market creators to issue "clarifications". Questions that allow updates will include the sentence in their ancillary data: "Updates made by the question creator via the bulletin board on 0x6A5D0222186C0FceA7547534cC13c3CFd9b7b6A4F74 should be considered. In summary, clarifications that do not impact the question's intent should be considered." Where the [transaction](https://polygonscan.com/tx/0xa14f01b115c4913624fc3f508f960f4dea252758e73c28f5f07f8e19d7bca066) reference outlining what outlining should be considered.

--------------------------------

### Resolution > UMA Optimistic Oracle Integration > Resolution Process > Possible Flows

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/resolution/UMA

When the first proposed price is disputed for a `questionID` on the adapter, a callback is made and posted as the reward for this new proposal. This means a second `questionID`, making a new `questionID` to the OO (the reward is returned before the callback is made and posted as the reward for this new proposal). This allows for a second round of resolution, and correspondingly a second dispute is required for it to go to the DVM. The thinking behind this is to doubles the cost of a potential griefing vector (two disputes are required just one) and also allows far-fetched (incorrect) first price proposals to not delay the resolution. As such there are two possible flows: Initialize (CTFAdapter) -> Propose (OO) -> Resolve (CTFAdapter), Initialize (CTFAdaptor) -> Propose (OO) -> Challenge (OO) -> Propose (OO) -> Resolve (CTFAdaptor), Initialize (CTFAdaptor) -> Propose (OO) -> Challenge (OO) -> Propose (OO) -> Challenge (CtfAdapter) -> Resolve (CTFAdaptor).

--------------------------------

### How to Fetch Markets > 1. Fetch by Slug

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/fetch-markets-guide

When you need to retrieve a specific market or event that you already know about, fetching by its unique slug identifier is the best approach. The slug can be found directly in the Polymarket frontend URL. From any Polymarket URL, the slug is the path segment after `/event/` or `/market/`. For example, in the URL `https://polymarket.com/event/fed-decision-in-october?tid=1758818660485`, the slug is `fed-decision-in-october`.

### Complete Example

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/quickstart

This example demonstrates how to create and post a buy order using the Polymarket CLOB client. It covers initializing the client with necessary credentials, including API keys and signature types, and then executing the order.

The TypeScript example shows the process using `ethers` for wallet management and the `@polymarket/clob-client` library. It involves creating a temporary client to obtain API credentials, then instantiating the main client with these credentials to place an order.

Similarly, the Python example utilizes the `py_clob_client` library. It follows a comparable flow, obtaining API credentials and then submitting a buy order with specified token ID, price, and size.

### Onchain Order Info

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/onchain-order-info

The `makerAssetId` and `takerAssetId` are crucial for understanding the direction of the trade. If `makerAssetId` is 0, it signifies a BUY order where the maker is giving USDC and receiving Outcome tokens. Conversely, if `makerAssetId` is non-zero, it's a SELL order, with the maker giving Outcome tokens and receiving USDC. Similarly, `takerAssetId` indicates the asset received by the taker. A `takerAssetId` of 0 means the taker is receiving USDC in a SELL order, while a non-zero ID means the taker is receiving Outcome tokens in a BUY order.

--------------------------------

### RTDS Comments > Message Format

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-comments

When subscribed to the `comments` topic with the `comment_created` type, you will receive messages containing detailed information about the newly created comment. The message includes the comment's `body`, `createdAt` timestamp, a unique `id`, and its relationship to a `parentCommentID` (if it's a reply) or `parentEntityID` and `parentEntityType` (if it's a top-level comment). It also includes `reactionCount`, `reportCount`, and user information such as their `profile` object, which contains fields like `baseAddress`, `displayUsernamePublic`, `name`, `proxyWallet`, and `pseudonym`. The `userAddress` indicates the Polygon address of the comment's author, and `replyAddress` is the Polygon address used for replies.

### Onchain Order Info

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/onchain-order-info

The `OrderFilled` event provides detailed information about an order that has been successfully filled on the blockchain. The `orderHash` uniquely identifies the specific order, while `maker` refers to the user who created the order and provided the funds. The `taker` is either the user who filled the order or the Exchange contract itself if multiple limit orders were involved in the fill.

The subscription can be further refined using optional filters to target specific comment IDs, users, or event types.

### Liquidity Rewards > Seeing Rewards in the Order Book > Viewing Rewards

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/liquidity-rewards

The total rewards, max spread, and minimum shares required to earn rewards vary by market. You can view the rewards for a given market in its Order Book. On the Polymarket order book, you can hover over the Rewards text to see the amount of rewards available in total on each market. The blue highlighted lines correspond to the max spread — meaning the farthest distance your limit order can be from the midpoint of the market to earn rewards. In the example below, because the max spread is 3c, every order within 3c of the midpoint is eligible for rewards. If the midpoint is < $0.10, you need to have orders on both sides to qualify.

### How to Fetch Markets > 3. Fetch All Active Markets

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/gamma-markets-api/fetch-markets-guide

When you need to retrieve all available active markets, typically for broader analysis or market discovery, the most efficient approach is to use the `/events` endpoint and work backwards, as events contain their associated markets. Key parameters for this endpoint include `order=id` to order by event ID, `ascending=false` to get the newest events first, `closed=false` to only retrieve active markets, and `limit` to control the response size. The `offset` parameter is used for pagination.

### Polymarket Changelog > May 28, 2025 > New FAK Order Type

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/changelog/changelog

A new order type, Fill and Kill (FAK), is being introduced. FAK orders function by filling as many shares as possible immediately at the specified price, with any remaining unfilled portion being canceled. This differs from Fill or Kill (FOK) orders, which require the entire order to be filled instantly or be canceled. FAK offers more flexibility by allowing partial fills.

### L1 Methods > Client Initialization

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/clients/methods-l1

L1 methods require the client to initialize with a signer. For example, in TypeScript, you would import `ClobClient` and `Wallet` from `ethers`. Then, create a `Wallet` instance using your private key (preferably from an environment variable for security) and pass this signer to the `ClobClient` constructor. This client instance, now configured with a signer, is ready for operations that require L1 authentication, such as creating user API credentials.

### Builder Signing Server > Configuration

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/builder-signing-server

To configure the signing server, create a `.env` file in the root directory with your Builder API credentials. The file should include `PORT`, `POLY_BUILDER_API_KEY`, `POLY_BUILDER_SECRET`, and `POLY_BUILDER_PASSPHRASE`. Never commit your `.env` file to version control; add it to `.gitignore` to prevent accidental exposure of your credentials. You can run the server on any port you choose, with the default being `5001`, by setting the `PORT` environment variable. Ensure your client applications are configured to use the same port.

--------------------------------

### Signature Types and Funder

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

When initializing the L2 client, specifying the **signatureType** and **funder** address is crucial. The `signatureType` can be EOA (0) for standard Ethereum wallets, POLY_PROXY (1) for custom proxy wallets used with Magic Link logins, or GNOSIS_SAFE (2) for Gnosis Safe multisig wallets. The funder address is the account that holds the funds and will pay gas for transactions. For EOA, the funder is the EOA address itself. For POLY_PROXY and GNOSIS_SAFE, the funder is the proxy wallet address.

--------------------------------

### REST API > L2 Authentication > What is L2?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

L2 authentication utilizes API credentials (apiKey, secret, passphrase) generated during L1 authentication. These credentials are used exclusively to authenticate requests made to the CLOB API, with requests signed using HMAC-SHA256. This level of authentication enables access to various L2 methods, including posting orders, viewing open orders, canceling orders, and retrieving trade information.

--------------------------------

### Liquidity Rewards > Equations

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

Q_normal represents the normalized point total for a specific sample, calculated by dividing a participant's Q_min by the sum of Q_min for all participants (N) in that market. This normalization ensures fair comparison across different participants. Q_epoch is the cumulative score over a 10,080-minute epoch (one week), calculated by summing the Q_normal values for each sample within that epoch. Finally, Q_final represents the final normalized score for an epoch, determined by dividing a participant's Q_epoch by the total Q_epoch of all participants.

--------------------------------

### How Are Markets Clarified? > Clarifications

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/how-are-markets-clarified

In rare cases, circumstances occur that were not foreseen at a market’s creation and it becomes necessary to clarify rules after trading has begun. In these cases Polymarket may issue an “Additional context” update to the rules. If you believe a clarification is necessary for a market, the best place to request a clarification is in the [Polymarket Discord](https://discord.com/invite/polymarket) **#market-review** channel.

--------------------------------

### RTDS Crypto Prices > Payload Fields

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-crypto-prices

The payload fields for both Binance and Chainlink crypto price messages are consistent in their naming but differ in symbol format. The `symbol` field indicates the trading pair, with Binance using lowercase concatenated pairs (e.g., "solusdt") and Chainlink using slash-separated pairs (e.g., "eth/usd"). The `timestamp` field provides the Unix milliseconds of the price data, and the `value` field is the current price in the quote currency.

--------------------------------

### L1 Methods > API Key Management > createOrDeriveApiKey()

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/clients/methods-l1

The `createOrDeriveApiKey()` method is a convenient way to manage your API keys. It first attempts to derive an API key using the default nonce. If no credentials exist for that nonce, it proceeds to create a new API key. This method is recommended for initial setup, especially when you are unsure whether API credentials have already been established for your wallet.

--------------------------------

### Builder Signing Server > Troubleshooting

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/builder-signing-server

If the server fails to start with an error like `Error: POLY_BUILDER_API_KEY environment variable is required`, ensure your `.env` file contains all the necessary variables: `POLY_BUILDER_API_KEY`, `POLY_BUILDER_SECRET`, and `POLY_BUILDER_PASSPHRASE`. If you encounter `Error: listen EADDRINUSE: address already in use :::5001`, change the port in your `.env` file (e.g., `PORT=5002`) and update your client configuration accordingly. For invalid signature errors, verify that the request body is correctly passed as a JSON string, that the path and method match the client's request exactly, and that both the server and client are using the same Builder API credentials.

--------------------------------

### REST API

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

For developers who prefer not to use the provided Python or TypeScript clients, direct REST API calls can be made. When using L2 authentication, specific headers must be included: `POLY_ADDRESS` (Polygon signer address), `POLY_SIGNATURE` (HMAC signature for the request), `POLY_TIMESTAMP` (current UNIX timestamp), `POLY_API_KEY` (user's API key), and `POLY_PASSPHRASE` (user's API passphrase). The `POLY_SIGNATURE` is an HMAC-SHA256 signature generated using the user's API secret.

--------------------------------

### Real Time Data Socket > Authentication

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-overview

The RTDS supports two types of authentication depending on the subscription type:

1. **CLOB Authentication**: Required for certain trading-related subscriptions
   * `key`: API key
   * `secret`: API secret
   * `passphrase`: API passphrase

2. **Gamma Authentication**: Required for user-specific data
   * `address`: User wallet address

### Polymarket Changelog > August 26, 2025 > Updated /trades and /activity endpoints

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/changelog/changelog

The maximum values for query parameters on the Data-API `/trades` and `/activity` endpoints have been reduced. The `limit` parameter now has a maximum value of 500, and the `offset` parameter has a maximum value of 1,000.

### Your First Order

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/quickstart/orders/first-order

The Python client can be initialized in three ways depending on your login method: using a Polymarket Proxy associated with an Email/Magic account (signature_type=1), using a Polymarket Proxy associated with a Browser Wallet like Metamask or Coinbase Wallet (signature_type=2), or trading directly from an EOA (signature_type not specified, for advanced users). You'll need to set your API credentials and then create and sign an order with the `OrderArgs` object, specifying the price, size, side, and token ID. Finally, post the signed order using `client.post_order` with the desired `OrderType` (e.g., `OrderType.GTC` for Good-Till-Cancelled).

--------------------------------

### Deployment and Additional Information > Deployment

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CTF/deployment-resources

The CTF contract is deployed and verified at specific addresses on the Polygon Mainnet. These addresses are crucial for interacting with the contract. Additionally, Polymarket offers code samples in both Python and TypeScript to facilitate this interaction. To utilize these samples, an RPC endpoint is necessary, and users will be responsible for gas fees associated with function calls. It is important to select the correct code example based on your wallet type (Safe Wallet or Proxy Wallet) for successful implementation.

--------------------------------

### Using the Order Book > Viewing the Order Book

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/using-the-orderbook

The order book is a list of every open order to buy or sell shares in a particular market. In the market for “Presidential Election Winner 2024”, when viewing the order book for Trump Yes shares, the green side represents the Bids: the highest price traders are willing to pay to buy Trump Yes shares. The red side represents the Asks: the lowest price traders are willing to accept to sell Trump Yes shares. Notice that there is a 0.3c gap between the highest bid and the lowest ask price. This is referred to as the spread.

--------------------------------

### L1 Methods > API Key Management > createApiKey()

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/clients/methods-l1

The `createApiKey()` method generates new API key credentials for your wallet signer. These credentials, comprising an `apiKey`, `secret`, and `passphrase`, are used for authenticated requests to L2 services. It's important to note that each wallet can only have one active API key at a time; creating a new key will automatically invalidate any previous one.

### How Do I Export My Key?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/how-to-export-private-key

Exporting your private key gives you direct control and security over your funds. This process is applicable if you’ve signed up via email.

**DO NOT** share your private key with other parties, platforms, or people. We will never ask for your private key.

1. Access the Export Link while signed into Polymarket: [https://reveal.magic.link/polymarket](https://reveal.magic.link/polymarket)
2. Sign-in on Magic.Link
3. Export Private Key. Once revealed, you should securely store the private key displayed, where others can’t access it.
4. Log out of Magic.Link

### Using Our SDKs

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/order-attribution

We strongly recommend using our official SDKs and server implementations for builder signing. You do not need to implement the signing logic yourself. The provided packages handle all signing and header injection, ensuring security and reliability. These packages include the core signing functionality, a production-ready remote signing server, and an updated CLOB client with built-in builder support.

--------------------------------

### RTDS Comments > Payload Fields > Profile Object Fields

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-comments

The `profile` object within a comment message provides detailed information about the user who authored the comment. `baseAddress` is the user's primary profile address. `displayUsernamePublic` is a boolean indicating whether their chosen username should be publicly displayed. `name` is the user's display name, while `proxyWallet` is the specific Polygon address used for transactions, which might differ from their `baseAddress`. `pseudonym` is a generated identifier for the user.

--------------------------------

### How Are Prediction Markets Resolved? > To propose a market resolution

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/how-are-markets-resolved

To propose a market resolution, navigate to the market you want to propose and click Resolution > Propose Resolution. You will be taken to the corresponding UMA oracle page for the market, which shows the bond required and reward for successful proposal. Ensure that you have enough USDC.e in your wallet on Polygon to supply the bond (usually $750). Select the outcome you would like to propose from the drop-down menu. Connect your wallet and submit the transaction. It will now enter the UMA Oracle’s verification queue.

--------------------------------

### CLOB Client

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

The CLOB client, available for both TypeScript and Python, facilitates trading by allowing users to create and post orders. It requires initialization with host details, chain ID, a signer (like an ethers.js Wallet or a private key), API credentials for L2 methods, a signature type, and a funder address. Once initialized, methods like `createAndPostOrder` can be used to execute trades.

--------------------------------

### How to Sign-Up > Email or Google Sign-Up

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/get-started/how-to-signup

Signing up for Polymarket with your email address or Google account is quick, simple, and secure. First, click **Sign Up** on the top right of the Polymarket homepage. Then, enter your email address and click **continue**. Alternatively, you can use your Google account to sign in and follow the same procedure. After that, you will need to **copy the security code** provided by Magic. You’ll receive an email with the subject “Log in to Polymarket”. Open the email, and click the **Log in to Polymarket** button. In the new window, enter or **paste the security code** from the previous step. You'll see a Login Complete message. Return to your original Polymarket window. Back on Polymarket, you'll be signed in. Choose your display name, agree to the terms of service, opt into email updates, and get started trading.

### REST API > L1 Authentication

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

While client libraries are recommended for signing and authentication, developers can make direct REST API calls with L1 authentication. This requires including specific headers in the request: `POLY_ADDRESS` (your Polygon signer address), `POLY_SIGNATURE` (the CLOB EIP 712 signature), `POLY_TIMESTAMP` (the current UNIX timestamp), and `POLY_NONCE` (a nonce, defaulting to 0).

### Place Single Order > Create and Place an Order

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/create-order

Create and place an order using the Polymarket CLOB API clients. All orders are represented as "limit" orders, but "market" orders are also supported. To place a market order, simply ensure your price is marketable against current resting limit orders, which are executed on input at the best price.

### L1 Methods > API Key Management > deriveApiKey()

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/clients/methods-l1

The `deriveApiKey()` method allows you to retrieve existing API key credentials (L2 credentials) by providing a specific nonce. If you have previously created API credentials using a particular nonce, this method will consistently return the same set of credentials. This is useful if you need to deterministically generate your API keys.

--------------------------------

### RTDS Comments > Message Types > comment_created

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-comments

The `comment_created` message type is triggered whenever a user posts a new comment, whether it's a standalone comment on an event or a reply to an existing comment. This allows you to capture and process new user-generated content in real-time. The `comment_removed` type signals that a comment has been deleted. Additionally, `reaction_created` and `reaction_removed` message types inform you about changes in user reactions to comments, providing insights into engagement.

--------------------------------

### Liquidity Rewards > Equations

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

The scoring function S(v, s) is defined as $(
rac{v-s}{v})^2 cdot b$, where 'v' represents the maximum spread from the midpoint in cents, 's' is the spread from the size-cutoff-adjusted midpoint, and 'b' is an in-game multiplier. This function is used to calculate the point totals for book one (Q_one) and book two (Q_two). Q_one sums the scoring function applied to the bid sizes across different spreads in both books, while Q_two does the same for ask sizes. The equations incorporate market complements (m') to account for both sides of the market.

--------------------------------

### Supported Symbols > Chainlink Source Symbols

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-crypto-prices

The Chainlink source supports cryptocurrency trading pairs using a slash-separated format. Examples include `btc/usd` for Bitcoin to USD, `eth/usd` for Ethereum to USD, `sol/usd` for Solana to USD, and `xrp/usd` for XRP to USD.

### Supported Symbols > Binance Source Symbols

The Binance source supports various cryptocurrency trading pairs using lowercase concatenated format. Examples include `btcusdt` for Bitcoin to USDT, `ethusdt` for Ethereum to USDT, `solusdt` for Solana to USDT, and `xrpusdt` for XRP to USDT.

### Place Single Order > Order types

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/orders/create-order

A Fill-Or-Kill order is a market order to buy (in dollars) or sell (in shares) shares that must be executed immediately in its entirety; otherwise, the entire order will be cancelled. A Fill-And-Kill order is a market order to buy (in dollars) or sell (in shares) that will be executed immediately for as many shares as are available; any portion not filled at once is cancelled. A Good-Til-Cancelled order is a limit order that is active until it is fulfilled or cancelled. A Good-Til-Date order is a type of order that is active until its specified date (UTC seconds timestamp), unless it has already been fulfilled or cancelled. There is a security threshold of one minute. If the order needs to expire in 90 seconds the correct expiration value is: now + 1 minute + 30 seconds

--------------------------------

### REST API > API Credentials > Create API Credentials

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

API credentials, consisting of an `apiKey`, `secret`, and `passphrase`, are required for L2 authentication. These credentials can be created via a POST request to `{clob-endpoint}/auth/api-key` or derived using a GET request to `{clob-endpoint}/auth/derive-api-key`. The response will contain all three values necessary for L2 authentication.

--------------------------------

### Steps

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

To boost two-sided liquidity, the system takes the minimum of the two calculated scores, $Q_{ne}$ and $Q_{no}$. This minimum value represents the rewarded score for two-sided liquidity. Additionally, one-sided liquidity is rewarded at a reduced rate, achieved by dividing the score by a factor 'c'. These calculations are performed every minute.

--------------------------------

### Real Time Data Socket > Subscription Management

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/RTDS/RTDS-overview

To subscribe to data streams, send a JSON message with this structure:

```json  theme={null}
{
  "action": "subscribe",
  "subscriptions": [
    {
      "topic": "topic_name",
      "type": "message_type",
      "filters": "optional_filter_string",
      "clob_auth": {
        "key": "api_key",
        "secret": "api_secret", 
        "passphrase": "api_passphrase"
      },
      "gamma_auth": {
        "address": "wallet_address"
      }
    }
  ]
}
```

To unsubscribe from data streams, send a similar message with `"action": "unsubscribe"`.

### Glossary > Token

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/quickstart/introduction/definitions

A token represents a stake in a specific Yes/No outcome in a Market. The price of a token can fluctuate between $0 - $1 based on the market belief in the outcome. When a market resolves, the token associated with the correct prediction can be redeemed for $1 USDC. This is also sometimes called an *Asset Id*.

### REST API > L1 Authentication > EIP-712 Signing Example

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

The `POLY_SIGNATURE` header is generated by signing a specific EIP-712 struct. This struct includes parameters such as the domain, its version, the chain ID (e.g., 137 for Polygon), and the values for address, timestamp, nonce, and a message attesting to wallet control. Reference implementations for generating this signature are available in both TypeScript and Python.

--------------------------------

### Liquidity Rewards > Methodology

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

The Polymarket liquidity rewards system calculates rewards based on a formula that values participation in markets, boosts two-sided depth (with single-sided orders also contributing), and considers the spread relative to the mid-market, adjusted by a size cutoff. Each market has defined parameters for the maximum spread and a minimum size cutoff for orders to be considered. The average rewards earned are determined by each participant's relative share of their Qn score within a specific market (m).

--------------------------------

### Steps

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

Finally, $Q_{final}$ normalizes $Q_{epoch}$ by dividing it by the sum of all other market makers' $Q_{epoch}$ scores within the same epoch. This normalized value is then multiplied by the total rewards available for the market to determine a trader's specific reward allocation for that epoch.

--------------------------------

### CLOB Client

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

Even with L2 authentication headers, methods that create user orders still require the user to sign the order payload. This ensures the integrity and authenticity of each trade initiated through the client.

### How Are Markets Disputed?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/dispute

Following the challenge period, a debate period of 24-48 hours commences. During this time, discussions take place, with voting occurring every other day, ensuring at least 24 hours for deliberation. Participants can contribute evidence and rationale in the Uma Discord server's #evidence-rationale and #voting-discussion channels. After the debate period concludes, UMA token holders cast their votes, a process that generally takes about 48 hours. This leads to one of four potential outcomes for the market resolution.

### Basic Setup

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/relayer-client

The relayer client is available for both TypeScript and Python, enabling interaction with the Polymarket relayer.

For TypeScript, you can use either Ethers v5 or Viem. Both versions require initializing a wallet and configuring builder credentials. The `RelayClient` can be initialized with the relayer URL, chain ID, wallet, and builder configuration. You can also explicitly specify the transaction type, such as `RelayerTxType.SAFE` for standard transactions or `RelayerTxType.PROXY` for Proxy Wallets (used by Magic Link users).

For Python, the `RelayClient` is initialized similarly, requiring the relayer URL, chain ID, private key, and a `BuilderConfig` object that includes builder credentials.

### Builder Profile & Keys > Obtaining Builder API Keys

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/builder-profile

Builder API keys are essential for attributing customer orders to your builder account. These credentials enable you to sign orders and include authentication headers in CLOB requests. You can create new API keys in the "Builder Keys" section of your profile. Each key comprises an `apiKey`, a `secret` for signing requests, and a `passphrase` for additional authentication. It is crucial to keep these keys secure and avoid exposing them in client-side code, recommending storage as environment variables and utilizing remote signing whenever feasible.

--------------------------------

### Authentication > L1 Authentication

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

L1 authentication uses the wallet's private key to sign an EIP-712 message used in the request header. It proves ownership and control over the private key. The private key stays in control of the user and all trading activity remains non-custodial.

--------------------------------

### CTF Operations

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/relayer-client

The relayer client enables you to execute Conditional Token Framework operations for your users. This includes actions like splitting positions.

--------------------------------

### Order Attribution > Signing Methods > Remote Signing (Recommended)

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/order-attribution

Remote signing is the recommended approach for protecting your Builder API credentials. With this method, your credentials never leave your secure server. Your customer signs an order payload, which is then sent to your builder signing server. This server uses your Builder API keys to cryptographically sign the entire payload and adds the authentication headers. The fully signed payload, signed by both your customer and you as the builder, is then sent to the CLOB. We provide a complete server implementation in the [@polymarket/builder-signing-server](https://github.com/Polymarket/builder-signing-server) repository.

--------------------------------

### Steps

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

The first market side score, denoted as $Q_{ne}$, is calculated by considering the trader's open bid and ask orders. For each order, a score is computed based on the difference between the maximum allowed spread (maxSpread config) and the order's spread relative to the adjusted market midpoint. The formula used is a quadratic function of this difference, weighted by the quantity of the order. This score is recalculated every minute using random sampling.

### Root > Troubleshooting > Error: NONCE_ALREADY_USED

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/clients/methods-l1

The `NONCE_ALREADY_USED` error signifies that the nonce you provided has already been utilized to create an API key. This method is crucial for obtaining the necessary API credentials for L2 authentication. Ensure that you call `createOrDeriveApiKey()` and then initialize the `ClobClient` with these credentials, as shown in the provided example snippet.

### Steps

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

Similarly, the second market side score, denoted as $Q_{no}$, is calculated. This score also takes into account the trader's open orders, applying a quadratic scoring rule that considers the spread relative to the adjusted market midpoint and the maximum spread configuration. Like $Q_{ne}$, $Q_{no}$ is also recalculated every minute using random sampling.

### Splitting USDC

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CTF/split

At any time, after a condition has been prepared on the CTF contract (via `prepareCondition`), it is possible to "split" collateral into a full (position) set. In other words, one unit USDC can be split into 1 YES unit and 1 NO unit. If splitting from the collateral, the CTF contract will attempt to transfer `amount` collateral from the message sender to itself. If successful, `amount` stake will be minted in the split target positions. If any of the transfers, mints, or burns fail, the transaction will revert. The transaction will also revert if the given partition is trivial, invalid, or refers to more slots than the condition is prepared with. This operation happens via the `splitPosition()` function on the CTF contract.

--------------------------------

### What is a Prediction Market? > Free-market trading

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/what-are-prediction-markets

You can buy or sell shares at any time before the event concludes, based on new information or changing circumstances. This flexibility allows the market prices to continuously reflect the most current and accurate probabilities.

### Root > Troubleshooting > Lost both credentials and nonce

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/clients/methods-l1

Unfortunately, if you have lost both your API credentials and the nonce, there is no method to recover your API credentials. In such a scenario, you will need to create entirely new credentials. Remember to save the nonce when creating new credentials to avoid future data loss.

### Merging Tokens

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CTF/merge

In addition to splitting collateral for a full set, the inverse can also happen; a full set can be "merged" for collateral. This operation can again happen at any time after a condition has been prepared on the CTF contract. One unit of each position in a full set is burned in return for 1 collateral unit. This operation happens via the `mergePositions()` function on the CTF contract.

--------------------------------

### Troubleshooting > Lost API credentials but have nonce

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

If you have lost your API credentials but still possess the nonce, you can recover them. Use the `deriveApiKey()` method, providing the original nonce as an argument. This will allow you to retrieve the previously generated API key and associated credentials.

### Holding Rewards > Total Position Value Computation

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/holding-rewards

The "Total Position Value" for each eligible polymarket is determined by evaluating your current holdings of "Yes" and "No" shares against the most recent mid-price for each outcome. For instance, if you hold 30,000 "Yes" shares at $0.53 and 10,000 "No" shares at $0.45, the Total Position Value is calculated as (30,000 * $0.53) + (10,000 * $0.45), which equals $15,900 + $4,500 = $20,400. The hourly holding reward is then calculated based on this total value and the annualized reward rate, divided by the number of days and hours in a year. For a 4.00% annual reward, the hourly reward would be approximately $20,400 * (0.04 / 365 / 24) ≈ $0.093.

--------------------------------

### Limit Orders > Managing limit orders

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/limit-orders

When you have an open order, you'll find it displayed just below the Order Book on the market's page. If you have open orders across multiple markets, you can easily manage and monitor them all from the [Portfolio page](https://polymarket.com/portfolio?tab=Open+orders).

Specifically for sports markets, any outstanding limit orders are automatically cancelled once the game begins, clearing the entire order book at the official start time. Be aware, game start times can shift so it’s important to always monitor your orders closely in case they are not cleared due to game changes or other circumstances.

Additionally, sports markets include a 3-second delay on the placement of marketable orders.

--------------------------------

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/what-are-prediction-markets

The price of shares in a prediction market represents the current probability of an event happening. For example, if shares of an event are trading at 20 cents, it indicates a 20% chance of that event occurring.

### Builder Signing Server > Client Integration

### Polymarket Bridge API > Bridge > Create deposit addresses

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/misc-endpoints/bridge-deposit

The Polymarket Bridge API facilitates the bridging of assets from various chains and their subsequent swapping to USDC.e on the Polygon network, which serves as the collateral for all trading activities on Polymarket. This process ensures a seamless trading experience by converting incoming assets into the preferred stablecoin format.

**How it works:**
1. Request deposit addresses for your Polymarket wallet.
2. Receive unique deposit addresses for each supported chain/token.
3. Send assets to the appropriate deposit address.
4. Assets are automatically bridged and swapped to USDC.e on Polygon.
5. USDC.e is credited to your Polymarket wallet for trading.

--------------------------------

### How Are Prices Calculated? > Initial Price

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/how-are-prices-calculated

The prices and probabilities displayed on Polymarket are determined by the midpoint of the bid-ask spread within the orderbook. When a market is first created, there are no shares and no pre-set prices. Market makers, who are traders placing limit orders, can set their desired prices for buying YES or NO shares. A trade occurs and establishes the initial market price when the offers for the YES and NO sides sum up to $1.00, signifying a match between a buyer and a seller.

For instance, if a limit order to buy YES shares is placed at $0.60, it will be matched when someone places a limit order to sell NO shares at $0.40. This transaction then sets the initial market price. It's important to note that Polymarket does not dictate prices; they are emergent from the collective willingness of users to buy and sell shares, with all trades occurring on a peer-to-peer basis.

--------------------------------

### How Are Prices Calculated? > Prices = Probabilities

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/how-are-prices-calculated

The probability displayed for a market is calculated as the midpoint between the bid and ask prices. For example, if the bid price for an outcome is $0.34 and the ask price is $0.40, the displayed probability is 37% (the midpoint). When the bid-ask spread is wider than $0.10, the probability is presented as the last traded price. It's important to understand that you may not be able to purchase shares at the exact displayed probability due to this bid-ask spread. In the example where the probability is 37%, a buyer would pay $0.40 per share for the available shares at that price, after which the price would increase for subsequent purchases.

--------------------------------

### How Are Markets Created?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/how-are-markets-created

Markets are created by the markets team with input from users and the community. While users cannot directly create their own markets, they are encouraged to suggest ideas for new markets. In choosing which markets to list, Polymarket considers factors such as sufficient demand for trading (targeting a minimum of $X in trading volume), social good or news value, clarity of resolution, credibility of the resolution source, and a definitive time frame for resolution.

--------------------------------

### Get daily builder volume time-series > OpenAPI > components > schemas > BuilderVolumeEntry > properties > activeUsers

Number of active users for this builder on this date

--------------------------------

### Understanding Prices

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/index

Prices = Probabilities. _Prices (odds) on Polymarket represent the current probability of an event occurring._ For example, in a market predicting whether the Miami Heat will win the 2025 NBA Finals, if YES shares are trading at 18 cents, it indicates a 18% chance of Miami winning. These odds are determined by what price other Polymarket users are currently willing to buy & sell those shares at. Just how stock exchanges don’t “set” the prices of stocks, Polymarket does not set prices / odds - they’re a function of supply & demand.

--------------------------------

### Root > Troubleshooting > Lost API credentials but have nonce

If you have lost your API credentials but still possess the nonce, you can recover your credentials by using the `deriveApiKey()` function along with the original nonce. This function allows you to reconstruct your API access using the stored nonce.

### How Are Markets Disputed?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/dispute

Anyone can dispute a proposed market resolution if they feel it was proposed in error. Once a market is proposed for resolution, it enters a challenge period lasting 2 hours. If no one challenges the proposal within this timeframe, the resolution is considered valid, and the proposer gets their bond back along with a reward. During the 2-hour challenge period, any user can dispute the proposal on the [UMA dapp](https://oracle.uma.xyz/) by posting a challenge bond equivalent to the proposer's bond amount (typically $750).

--------------------------------

### Liquidity Rewards

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/liquidity-rewards

With Polymarket's Liquidity Rewards Program, you can earn money by placing limit orders that help keep the market active and balanced. The closer your orders are to the market's average price, the more you earn. The reward amount depends on how helpful your orders are in terms of size and pricing compared to others. The more competitive your limit orders, the more you can make. You get paid daily based on how much your orders add to the market, and can use our [Rewards page](https://polymarket.com/rewards) to check your current earnings for the day, which markets have rewards in place, as well as how much. The minimum reward payout is $1; amounts below this will not be paid. Simply put, the more you help the market by placing good orders, the more rewards you earn!

### Troubleshooting > Order rejected: insufficient balance

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/quickstart

When an order is rejected due to insufficient balance, it means the funder address does not have the required assets for the trade. For BUY orders, you need to have **USDC** in your funder address. For SELL orders, you must possess the **outcome tokens** of the market you are trading. You can verify your current balances by visiting your portfolio page on polymarket.com/portfolio.

--------------------------------

### Liquidity Rewards > Equations

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

The calculation of Q_min, which determines the minimum point total for scoring, depends on the market's midpoint. If the midpoint is within the range [0.10, 0.90], single-sided liquidity can score, with Q_min calculated as the maximum of the minimum of Q_one and Q_two, and the result of dividing the larger of Q_one or Q_two by 'c' (a scaling factor). However, if the midpoint falls outside this range (i.e., [0, 0.10) or (.90, 1.0]), liquidity must be double-sided to score, meaning Q_min is simply the minimum of Q_one and Q_two.

--------------------------------

### Relayer Client > Wallet Types

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/relayer-client

The Relayer Client supports two types of wallets: Safe Wallets and Proxy Wallets.

Safe Wallets are Gnosis Safe-based proxy wallets and require explicit deployment using `client.deploy()` before first use. They are the default wallet type when not specified.

Proxy Wallets are custom Polymarket proxy wallets that auto-deploy on the first transaction, meaning no `deploy()` call is needed. These are used for Magic Link users who authenticate via email/Google on Polymarket.com.

--------------------------------

### Steps

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/rewards/overview

The $Q_{normal}$ score is then determined by normalizing a market maker's minimum score ($Q_{min}$) by the sum of all other market makers' $Q_{min}$ scores within a given sample. This step normalizes individual performance against the collective activity.

--------------------------------

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/holding-rewards

To maintain accurate long-term pricing, Polymarket offers a 4.00% annualized Holding Reward calculated on the total value of your positions in certain polymarkets. A new reward and oracle-resolution system is planned for later this year, which will include a straightforward 1-click migration for existing rewards.

--------------------------------

### How Are Markets Disputed? > Outcomes

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/markets/dispute

There are four possible outcomes after the dispute process:

*   **Proposer wins**: The proposer's bond is returned, and they receive half of the disputer's bond as a bounty. The disputer forfeits their bond.
*   **Disputer wins**: The disputer's bond is returned, and they receive half of the proposer's bond as a bounty. The proposer forfeits their bond.
*   **Too Early**: This outcome applies when the underlying event has not yet occurred, such as a sports match that is still in progress. The disputer's bond is returned, and they get half of the proposer's bond as a bounty, while the proposer loses their bond.
*   **Unknown/50-50**: This rarely used outcome is for situations where none of the other options are suitable. In such cases, the market resolves to a 50% yes and 50% no split. The disputer's bond is returned, and they receive half of the proposer's bond as a bounty, with the proposer forfeiting their bond.

--------------------------------

### Troubleshooting > Order rejected: insufficient allowance

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/quickstart

An order rejection due to insufficient allowance signifies that the Exchange contract has not been granted permission to spend your tokens. If you are integrating programmatically, you may need to explicitly use the CTF contract's `setApprovalForAll()` method to grant the necessary permissions.

### Limit Orders > What are Limit Orders?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/limit-orders

To create a limit order:

1. In the buy modal, select **limit** in the order type dropdown.
2. Enter the price you are willing to buy (or sell, if you’ve selected to sell) shares at.
3. Enter the number of shares you want to buy or sell at that price. You can also optionally set an expiration date for your limit order, meaning it will be canceled if it doesn't execute within that timeframe.
4. Click **Buy** and confirm the transaction in your wallet.

Your limited orders that have yet to be filled are called "Open Orders".

Then, choose your preferred wallet and follow the prompts to connect it to Polymarket. Ensure you are connected to the Polygon Network; your wallet may prompt you to switch networks. Finally, sign the transaction prompt(s) on your wallet app or extension. You're signed in! Choose your display name, agree to the terms of service, opt into email updates, and start trading.

--------------------------------

### How Are Prices Calculated? > Future Price

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/how-are-prices-calculated

Similar to stock markets, prices on Polymarket fluctuate based on real-time supply and demand dynamics. The displayed probability of an outcome is generally the midpoint between the highest bid and the lowest ask for that outcome's shares. However, if the difference between the bid and ask prices (the spread) exceeds $0.10, the probability shown will be the last traded price instead of the midpoint. This ensures that the displayed probability remains a reasonable reflection of recent market activity, even when liquidity is lower.

### Troubleshooting > What's my funder address?

--------------------------------

### What is Polymarket? > Understanding Prices

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/get-started/what-is-polymarket

Prices (odds) on Polymarket represent the current probability of an event occurring. For example, in a market predicting whether the Miami Heat will win the 2025 NBA Finals, if YES shares are trading at 18 cents, it indicates a 18% chance of Miami winning. These odds are determined by what price other Polymarket users are currently willing to buy & sell those shares at. Just how stock exchanges don't "set" the prices of stocks, Polymarket does not set prices / odds - they're a function of supply & demand.

--------------------------------

### What is a Prediction Market? > Making predictions

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/what-are-prediction-markets

If you believe the actual probability of an event is higher than the market price suggests, you can buy shares. For instance, if you think a team has a better than 20% chance of winning, you would buy shares at 20 cents. If the event occurs, each share becomes worth $1, yielding a profit.

### Polymarket vs. Polling

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/polling

While legacy polls capture a snapshot of opinion at a specific moment, they are often outdated by the time they're published—sometimes lagging by several days. In contrast, Polymarket reflects real-time sentiment as events unfold, offering continuous updates and a more dynamic understanding of public opinion.

Studies show that prediction markets like Polymarket tend to outperform traditional pollsters because participants are financially incentivized to be correct. This creates more thoughtful, data-driven predictions. Research by James Surowiecki, author of The Wisdom of Crowds, has highlighted how markets like these can be more accurate than polls due to the "collective intelligence" of diverse participants. Additionally, the Iowa Electronic Markets, an academic research project at the University of Iowa, has consistently demonstrated the superior accuracy of prediction markets like Polymarket over traditional polling in predicting political outcomes.

Polymarket provides a constantly updating picture of public sentiment, offering a degree of accuracy and timeliness that traditional pollsters, who typically report data that is days old, simply cannot match.

--------------------------------

### Redeeming Tokens

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CTF/redeem

Once a condition has had its payouts reported (ie by the UMACTFAdapter calling `reportPayouts` on the CTF contract), users with shares in the winning outcome can redeem them for the underlying collateral. Specifically, users can call the `redeemPositions` function on the CTF contract which will burn all valuable conditional tokens in return for collateral according to the reported payout vector.

### Can I Sell Early?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/sell-early

Yes, you can sell or close your position early. You may sell shares at any point before the market is resolved by either placing a market order to sell shares at the prevailing bid price in the orderbook, or by placing a limit order for how many shares you wish to sell and at what price. The limit order will only be executed if/when there is a willing buyer for your shares at the price you set.

### What is Polymarket?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/get-started/what-is-polymarket

Polymarket is the world’s largest prediction market, allowing you to stay informed and profit from your knowledge by betting on future events across various topics. Studies show prediction markets are often more accurate than pundits because they combine news, polls, and expert opinions into a single value that represents the market's view of an event's odds. Our markets reflect *accurate, unbiased, and real-time probabilities* for the events that matter most to you. Markets seek truth.

### Troubleshooting > Error: INVALID_SIGNATURE

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

If you encounter an `INVALID_SIGNATURE` error, it indicates that your wallet's private key is incorrect or improperly formatted. To resolve this, you should verify that your private key is a valid hex string (it must start with "0x"). Additionally, ensure you are using the correct private key for the intended address and that the key has the necessary permissions.

--------------------------------

### Limit Orders > What are Limit Orders?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/limit-orders

Limit orders are open orders (pending trades) that only execute when the market trades at your desired price.

For example, if the highest you’re willing to pay for a share of Trump “Yes” in the 2024 Republican Nomination is 72c, but the current market price is 73c, you could create a limit order at 72c and wait until someone is willing to sell Yes shares at your desired price.

It’s not necessary for the entire order to execute at once. Limit orders can ‘partially fill’ as individual traders fill parts of your order.

--------------------------------

### Why Crypto?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/why-do-i-need-crypto

Polymarket operates on Polygon, a proof-of-stake layer two blockchain built on [Ethereum](https://ethereum.org). All transactions are denominated in USDC, a US-dollar pegged stablecoin. This architecture offers several advantages over traditional prediction markets.

--------------------------------

### Why Crypto? > Why USDC? > Global Reach

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/why-do-i-need-crypto

Research has shown that wide availability of prediction markets increases their accuracy. Using decentralized blockchain technology removes the need for a central authority in trading, which fosters fairness and open participation around the globe.

### Is My Money Safe? > Keep your private keys private.

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/is-my-money-safe

Losing your private key or passwords can result in losing access to your funds. It's crucial to store this information in a safe and secure environment.

--------------------------------

### Does Polymarket Have Trading Limits?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/no-limits

By design, the Polymarket orderbook **does not** have trading size limits. It matches willing buyers and sellers of any amount.

However, there is no guarantee that it will be possible to transact a desired amount of shares without impacting the price significantly, or at all if there are no willing counterparties. Before trading in any market, especially in large size, it is valuable to look at the orderbook to understand depth of liquidity, ie how many buyers or sellers are in the market and their desired trade size and price.

--------------------------------

### Relayer Client > Wallet Types > Proxy Wallets

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/relayer-client

Proxy Wallets are custom Polymarket proxy wallets. They auto-deploy on the first transaction, eliminating the need for an explicit `deploy()` call. These wallets are particularly useful for Magic Link users who authenticate through Polymarket.com. Like Safe Wallets, they handle gasless transactions paid by Polymarket, transaction execution, ERC20 approvals, and CTF operations.

### Remote Signing

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/relayer-client

For enhanced security, Polymarket supports remote signing. This feature allows you to keep your builder credentials on a secure server, rather than directly in your client application. To enable remote signing, you configure the `BuilderConfig` with a `remoteBuilderConfig` object, specifying the URL of your remote signing service.

This approach is supported for both TypeScript and Python.

This approach gives you full control over your assets, providing protection against potential security threats like hacks, misuse, and unauthorized transactions.

### API Rate Limits > How Rate Limiting Works

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/quickstart/introduction/rate-limits

All rate limits are enforced using Cloudflare's throttling system. When you exceed the maximum configured rate for any endpoint, requests are throttled rather than immediately rejected. This means that requests over the limit are delayed or queued rather than dropped. Some endpoints also allow short bursts above the sustained rate, and limits reset based on sliding time windows, such as per 10 seconds or per minute.

--------------------------------

### Holding Rewards

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/trading/holding-rewards

The current Holding Reward rate is set at 4.00% and applies to all eligible positions. This rate is variable and can be changed at Polymarket's discretion. Polymarket also reserves the right to impose limits on the total rewards distributed. The rewards are currently funded by the Polymarket Treasury. Your total position value is sampled hourly, with rewards distributed daily. The calculation is based on the value of your eligible positions at the time of each hourly evaluation.

--------------------------------

### How to Deposit > Depositing funds on Polymarket > How to purchase and deposit USDC

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/get-started/how-to-deposit

USDC is available on most major exchanges, including Coinbase. If your exchange supports sending or withdrawing to Polygon, we recommend this option for faster and fee-free transactions. Alternatively, you can deposit USDC via the Ethereum network.

--------------------------------

### What is a Prediction Market?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/what-are-prediction-markets

A prediction market is a platform where people can bet on the outcome of future events. By buying and selling shares in the outcomes, participants collectively forecast the likelihood of events such as sports results, political elections, or entertainment awards.

--------------------------------

### Deposit USDC on Ethereum

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/deposits/usdc-on-eth

Depositing USDC on the Ethereum network to Polymarket will automatically bridge your funds to the Polygon network. This means that when you initiate a deposit from Ethereum, Polymarket handles the process of transferring your USDC to the Polygon network, making it readily available for trading within your Polymarket account on Polygon. This seamless bridging simplifies the process for users who wish to trade on Polygon but hold their assets on Ethereum.

--------------------------------

### Making money on markets

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/index

In the example above, if you believe Miami’s chances of winning are higher than 18%, you would buy “Yes” shares at 18 cents each. If Miami wins, each “Yes” share would be worth $1, resulting in an 82-cent profit per share. Conversely, any trader who owned “No” shares would see their investment become worthless once the game is over. Since it’s a market, you’re not locked into your trade. You can sell your shares at any time at the current market price. As the news changes, the supply and demand for shares fluctuates, causing the share price to reflect the new odds for the event.

--------------------------------

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/get-started/how-to-deposit

MoonPay enables you to buy USDC (on Polygon) using your Visa, Mastercard, and select bank cards. Please be aware that payment options and transaction limits may vary depending on your region. [How to use MoonPay](../deposits/moonpay/)

### Large Cross Chain Deposits

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/deposits/large-cross-chain-deposits

For deposits exceeding $50,000, it is recommended to utilize bridges to minimize fees and slippage. Ensure that you bridge your funds to your Polymarket USDC (Polygon) deposit address. Be aware that slippage can occur during the bridging transaction, and users should review the terms of use for any third-party bridge services.

### Troubleshooting > Error: Invalid Funder Address

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/CLOB/authentication

An `Invalid Funder Address` error suggests that your funder address is incorrect or does not align with your wallet. To resolve this, first check your Polymarket profile address on the Polymarket settings page ([polymarket.com/settings](https://polymarket.com/settings)). If the address doesn't exist or you've never logged into Polymarket.com, you'll need to deploy your address first before proceeding to create L2 authentication.

--------------------------------

### Builder Signing Server > Why Use Remote Signing?

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/developers/builders/builder-signing-server

Remote signing provides enhanced security by isolating credentials so your Builder API keys never leave your secure server. It also allows for centralized key management, enabling you to manage credentials in one secure location, and reduces exposure by not requiring client applications to have direct access to sensitive keys.

### Recover Missing Deposit > Recover on Polygon

Source: https://docs.polymarket.com/polymarket-learn/FAQ/recover-missing-deposit

For recovering a deposit made to the wrong token on the Polygon network, utilize the dedicated recovery tool located at https://matic-recovery.polymarket.com/. Log in with your Polymarket account credentials or by connecting your Polymarket wallet. After successful login, choose the asset that was mistakenly deposited. The system will then show you the balance of the incorrect asset and offer the functionality to recover these funds to a wallet of your choice.
